### [242] [Conditional Flow Matching for Continuous Anomaly Detection in Autonomous Driving on a Manifold-Aware Spectral Space](https://arxiv.org/abs/2602.17586)
*Antonio Guillen-Perez*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Unsupervised anomaly detection for safety-critical AV validation using OT-CFM with a PCA bottleneck, enabling stable log-likelihood estimates and kinematic-aware sampling. Demonstrates detectability of rare long-tail events on WOMD with AUC-ROC 0.766; highlights a predictability gap between kinematic danger and semantic non-compliance.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Scale safety validation for Level-4 autonomous vehicles by modeling the continuous density of expert driving and detecting rare, high-risk long-tail scenarios that rule-based heuristics miss.

Method: Optimal Transport Conditional Flow Matching (OT-CFM) constrained by a low-rank PCA bottleneck to ensure kinematic smoothness; exact Jacobian trace for deterministic log-likelihood; Early Fusion Transformer encoder with lane-aware goal conditioning and a skip-connection to the flow head; kinematic complexity weighting using path tortuosity and jerk; simulation-free training; evaluation on Waymo Open Motion Dataset.

Result: AUC-ROC of 0.766 on a heuristic golden set of safety-critical events; identifies out-of-distribution behaviors (e.g., lane-boundary violations, non-normative junction maneuvers) as a predictability gap not captured by traditional safety filters.

Conclusion: Deep-Flow provides a rigorous, data-driven foundation for statistical safety gates in autonomous fleets, enabling objective validation and highlighting the distinction between kinematic danger and semantic non-compliance.

Abstract: Safety validation for Level 4 autonomous vehicles (AVs) is currently bottlenecked by the inability to scale the detection of rare, high-risk long-tail scenarios using traditional rule-based heuristics. We present Deep-Flow, an unsupervised framework for safety-critical anomaly detection that utilizes Optimal Transport Conditional Flow Matching (OT-CFM) to characterize the continuous probability density of expert human driving behavior. Unlike standard generative approaches that operate in unstable, high-dimensional coordinate spaces, Deep-Flow constrains the generative process to a low-rank spectral manifold via a Principal Component Analysis (PCA) bottleneck. This ensures kinematic smoothness by design and enables the computation of the exact Jacobian trace for numerically stable, deterministic log-likelihood estimation. To resolve multi-modal ambiguity at complex junctions, we utilize an Early Fusion Transformer encoder with lane-aware goal conditioning, featuring a direct skip-connection to the flow head to maintain intent-integrity throughout the network. We introduce a kinematic complexity weighting scheme that prioritizes high-energy maneuvers (quantified via path tortuosity and jerk) during the simulation-free training process. Evaluated on the Waymo Open Motion Dataset (WOMD), our framework achieves an AUC-ROC of 0.766 against a heuristic golden set of safety-critical events. More significantly, our analysis reveals a fundamental distinction between kinematic danger and semantic non-compliance. Deep-Flow identifies a critical predictability gap by surfacing out-of-distribution behaviors, such as lane-boundary violations and non-normative junction maneuvers, that traditional safety filters overlook. This work provides a mathematically rigorous foundation for defining statistical safety gates, enabling objective, data-driven validation for the safe deployment of autonomous fleets.

</details>


### [243] [Graph Neural Model Predictive Control for High-Dimensional Systems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2602.17601)
*Patrick Benito Eberhard,Luis Pabon,Daniele Gammelli,Hugo Buurmeijer,Amon Lahr,Mark Leone,Andrea Carron,Marco Pavone*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: A graph-neural-network dynamics model combined with a structure-exploiting MPC and a linear-time state-condensing algorithm enables real-time control of 1,000-node soft robots at 100 Hz, achieving sub-centimeter tracking and obstacle avoidance, outperforming baselines by ~63.6%.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: High-dimensional soft-robot systems require accurate yet tractable dynamics models for real-time control. Dense MPC formulations struggle with scalability; exploiting local interactions via graphs and specialized condensing can preserve sparsity and enable real-time computation.

Method: Represent the system as a graph capturing localized interactions and train/use a Graph Neural Network to model dynamics while preserving sparsity. Apply a structure-exploiting Model Predictive Control with a dedicated condensing algorithm that eliminates state variables; complexity scales linearly with the number of nodes. Leverage GPU parallelization for real-time performance. Validate in simulation and on a physical soft robotic trunk.

Result: Demonstrates scalability to 1,000 nodes at 100 Hz in closed loop. Achieves sub-centimeter tracking accuracy on hardware. Outperforms baselines by 63.6%. Also shows capability for full-body obstacle avoidance.

Conclusion: The integration of GNN-based dynamics with a structure-exploiting MPC and linear-time condensing provides a scalable, real-time control framework for high-dimensional systems, particularly soft robots, with robust tracking and obstacle avoidance capabilities.

Abstract: The control of high-dimensional systems, such as soft robots, requires models that faithfully capture complex dynamics while remaining computationally tractable. This work presents a framework that integrates Graph Neural Network (GNN)-based dynamics models with structure-exploiting Model Predictive Control to enable real-time control of high-dimensional systems. By representing the system as a graph with localized interactions, the GNN preserves sparsity, while a tailored condensing algorithm eliminates state variables from the control problem, ensuring efficient computation. The complexity of our condensing algorithm scales linearly with the number of system nodes, and leverages Graphics Processing Unit (GPU) parallelization to achieve real-time performance. The proposed approach is validated in simulation and experimentally on a physical soft robotic trunk. Results show that our method scales to systems with up to 1,000 nodes at 100 Hz in closed-loop, and demonstrates real-time reference tracking on hardware with sub-centimeter accuracy, outperforming baselines by 63.6%. Finally, we show the capability of our method to achieve effective full-body obstacle avoidance.

</details>
